< Review>
I went to Bootie on March 10th. It was my first time, and it was a blast. The house band were really awesome, the mashups were great.

The place got a little too crowded for my liking at about 11:30. I stuck to the upstairs lounge which was nice and the bartender there was very kind.

I thought the crowd would be a bit older, but it was fine how it was, everyone was having a good time.<//Review>

<text>First, I want to clarify that this was my first time visiting this place. These are my first impressions based on my experience at this restaurant. Before, I review their food I do want to say that the guy at the cashier taking our orders was polite and respectful. The food on the other hand was horrible. The Teriyaki Chicken Bowl that we ordered was over loaded with teriyaki sauce. Second, and most importantly, the chicken smelled offputting. The smell of raw old chicken meat was overwhelmingly strong  as if the chicken was starting to go bad. So, this was a total fail for us. We didn't even touch this dish due to that, so we ended up throwing it away. Now the Vegetable Lo Mein plate wasn't as bad, but did have its' issues as well. For starters, it had way too much oil/sauce pooling at the bottom of the dish. It almost seemed like a noodle soup more than anything. Second, this dish tasted too sweet, but I think this is due to the excessive amount of sauce it had. Third, for being called a vegetable lo mein, I personally didn't feel like there were enough vegetables in this dish. Lastly, were ordered around $20 worth of food for it to end up being thrown away. I honestly don't think we'll be returning to this place. But these are my own personal opinions and impressions, but feel free to give it a try.<//text><pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNUnIzFAYWnJa9RlCHNAkfE1qmPkAR39VyXFXRH=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipO3eymtRkI91YNZEnttLh1t9zRA0nhW4aIIe-NV=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /pics>< Response>

<userid>112305216117231571390< /userid><user_name>Jodi Linwood< /user_name>< Time>
1608123658119<//Time>
<Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
Portion size. YUP. Unlimited Ban Chan. YUP. Great for my sick friend. YUP.

We wanted army stew, and looked for places around us. This happens to be one of the many few places(in the area) that actually have this stew, in comparison to all the existing kbbq places.

We got the hot pot - Base Army Stew(w/ serving size for two) and we were absolutely demolished. If you consider the ban chan and the red bean rice they give you, that's an insane amount of food that I think could have filled up to 3, maybe even 4 people.

They did not skip out on the sausage at all, and they have fish cake for sides. Tons and tons of protein!

This is a hole in the wall gem that blessed my sick friend's sinuses, maybe it'll gain more popularity as army stew becomes as popular as Korean barbecue.</text>

< username>
Timothy Kim<//username>
<Time>1528063619696</Time><Rating>4< /Rating><text>This place is a small local Korean restaurant that serves very basic, but hearty food. These types of restaurants are tradition for many Korean families who simply don't want to cook that day. The army stew is very cheap and tastes great. You won't get a value item like this in many American places so just give it a try. The food comes out fast but don't go into Korean restaurants expecting the best service. The best service is relative because there are different styles of what is good. In Korea, the style of good service is to not bother the table unless they call for you. I personally don't like cheese in my army stew because it makes the soup too creamy, but if you like creaminess cheese is the way to go. Other than this, I can see myself coming back.< /text>< Pics>

(Translated by Google) The food is generally tasty and delicious in homestyle style. Grilled fish, bulgogi, gondola soup and miso jjigae were very impressive. Unfortunately, lunch seems to lack a lot of side dishes. On the other hand, the lunch price is very good. I thought the gondre salmon roe was a signature menu here and I thought it was a signature menu here, but the soup stew is very popular! Anyway, it is a restaurant that is regarded as a Korean style restaurant which is colorful but does not have to be colorful.

Update..

Of all the boutiques in Fashion Valley, Burberry's floor plan/selection has you feeling like you discovered something new with each section that you enter. I'm a huge fan of their tailored trenchcoats. In my collection, my current favorite is the London Kensington (Leather Trim) Double Breasted Trench Coat, in Navy. <user>113266336642580442511</user>< name>

< time>
1574317724054</time>
<rate>5</rate>< review>
Aladdin's definitely has the market cornered on Mediterranean food in San Diego. It's often a favorite for a Sunday lunch with my family.

While the location is convenient to the 805 freeway, the parking can be a hassle. It shares the parking lot with other businesses, and while it looks large, it's surprisingly small. The restaurant is super casual, but it feels nice and open. It's always clean, and inviting.

You can't beat the food there. We usually get the Meza Platter - a dish that comes with 8 small dishes that includes hummus, babaganoush, chicken, lamb, and a bunch of other things, along with a pizza. The baklava is great too. Served with ice cream. These three things fed 5 hungry adults. Service is standard and prices are very reasonable.

This place could easily host large parties and kids are always welcomed there.

I always look forward to going to Aladdin's.< /review>

< Text>
I don't know where to begin. My wife ordered the lentil soup. It was pureed. I've never had pureed lentils at a Mediterranean restaurant. Maybe I've been eating at inauthentic restaurants or maybe this was just not prepared in the traditional manner. I ordered a chicken shawarma sandwich. It was not only greasy, dripping with brown oil, but covered in some indescribable sauce - one I've never had in 53 years of eating Mediterranean food. There were no tomatoes, lettuce or any type of yogurt-based sauce that I've always seen served with shawarma. Again, maybe I've had inauthentic food. Finally, the dolma were the type that have been marinated in tomato sauce. I prefer them without sauce, so this is a preference issue rather than one of authenticity. Regardless, they were not my favorite. Ultimately, this was not a good experience for us, and I don't intend to return.< /Text>

We ordered mix grill, French fries, and motabbal. The meats were seasoned & cooked perfectly. The French fries was Crispy and soft (it had alot of oil though). And the motabbal was just on point, no excess oil, not too little. However, the service were either annoying or careless. We had two servers apparently a Mexican women and an Asian man. In short: great food, shabby service.< /review>

Tricia Pooladi</name>
<Date>1551755325411</Date><rate>3<//rate>< review>
Cute atmosphere, wide selection of herbal teas and Mediterranean foods. They have hookah, so I think it's a hookah bar at night. The falafel appetizer was really delicious. I wish they served it Amsterdam Falafel style (WDC friends know what I'm talking about). Comes with pita triangles and tahini. I ordered a Greek salad, and the Greek salad was very good - I made little falafel pitas with the salad.
Mylo got the Fatoush salad, and it looked a little lacking - seemed to be light on the s'mac but they were really skimpy on the pita chips and didn't have feta on it although you can add it. Salad itself was large. Dave got the lamb schwarma and he said it was good. It came with a nice little greek salad, but I will have to try the schwarma for myself -- looked like it might be dry. Turkish coffee is delicious. Has a bit of minty flavor, which was quite pleasant.

Meal menu is a bit overpriced, service can be slow.<//review>
